In  \nChapter 5, we focus on critical aspects such as security \nand performance. Explore secrets management, state \nmanagement, disaster recovery, and tools like Secret \nManager, Identity and Access Management (IAM), and \nRole-Based Access Control (RBAC).\n• Collaboration and Automation: Effective \nmanagement thrives on teamwork and automation. \nThe final chapter covers how to collaborate efficiently, \nintegrate testing to boost performance, and automate \nyour infrastructure processes. We also provide best \npractices and industry insights to enhance your IaC \nexpertise.\nThis book isn’t just about commands and examples—it’s a thorough \nguide that will help you understand IaC and Terraform deeply, apply \nthese concepts effectively, and build secure, scalable, and efficient cloud \ninfrastructure.\n How to\xa0Use This Book\nThis guide is crafted to be a flexible learning tool tailored to your needs, \nregardless of your experience level. Here’s how to navigate it based on your \nbackground:\n• For Beginners in Cloud and IaC (Chapters 1––3): \nStart with the basics in Chapter 1, which introduces \nIaC and its advantages. You'll see how IaC improves \nefficiency, repeatability, and collaboration in \ninfrastructure management. Chapters 2 and 3 build \nyour practical skills with Terraform, teaching you PrefaCe\nxviiiinstallation and key commands. These chapters will \ngive you the confidence to manage infrastructure \nthrough code.\n• For Experienced Terraform Users Seeking GCP \nExpertise (Chapter 4): If you’re already familiar with \nTerraform, jump to Chapter 4. This chapter features \n18 detailed examples of provisioning essential GCP \ncomponents, from compute engines and networks to \nstorage and Kubernetes clusters.\n• For Advanced Users: Enhancing Security, \nPerformance, and Automation (Chapters 5  \nand 6): If you have a solid grasp of Terraform and \nwant to advance further, Chapters 5 and 6 are for you. \nChapter 5 covers security and performance topics, \nincluding secrets management, state management, and \ndisaster recovery. Chapter 6 focuses on optimization \nand collaboration, exploring testing, automation, \nand best practices to streamline your workflows and \nenhance team productivity.\n• Learning at Your Own Pace: Feel free to move around \nthe chapters based on your current knowledge and \ninterests. As cyber threats grow in complexity and frequency, traditional defence systems are struggling to keep pace. The introduction of artificial intelligence (AI) into cybersecurity marks a pivotal shift in the research and industry, allowing for faster, more adaptive, and more effi -\ncient threat management than ever before. AI-driven cybersecurity is not merely a technology upgrade; it represents a fundamental transformation in how digital ecosystems are safeguarded. By leveraging AI, cybersecu-rity teams can address the speed, scale, and sophistication required to combat today’s threats, providing organizations with the ability to stay ahead of attackers.\nAI’s capabilities in cybersecurity extend far beyond simple automation. \nThrough techniques such as machine learning (ML), deep learning, and the use of large language models (LLMs), AI systems are now capable of detecting intricate patterns and anomalies that may indicate cyber threats. With AI, defence mechanisms are not only automated but can also adapt in real time, responding to emerging threats as they evolve. This level of intelligence in cybersecurity allows organizations to manage risks proac -\ntively rather than reactively, reducing vulnerabilities and enhancing system resilience.\nThis book delves into the revolutionary ways in which AI-driven innova -\ntions are enhancing every aspect of cybersecurity, from threat detection and response automation to risk management and endpoint protection. As AI continues to develop, the synergy between cybersecurity and AI promises to reshape the landscape of digital defence, providing the tools needed to tackle complex, evolving cyber threats. For professionals, researchers, and decision-makers, understanding and leveraging AI in cybersecurity is not just advantageous; it’s essential for building robust, future-proof defences in a world where digital security is paramount.Preface\n\nviii Preface\nLet’s take a closer look at the specific themes and contributions of each \nchapter:\nChapter\xa01: Introduces AI’s role in cybersecurity, He served in the organizing committees of IEEE WF-IoT, IEEE ISCAS, IEEE ICIP, IEEE SiPS, IEEE MWSCAS, and GIoTS. In addi -\ntion, he taught many short IoT courses in different countries. He was the keynote speaker for many international conferences and conducted many webinars. He is currently the IEEE Northeast Michigan section chair and IEEE SPS Internet of Things (IoT) SIG Member. In the last few years, Dr. Abdelgawad was listed in the world’s top 2% of scientists by Stanford University, USA. In addition, Dr. Abdelgawad served as a prin -\ncipal investigator and co-principal investigator for several funded grants from the National Science Foundation.\nxiiVasavi Sravanthi Balusa\nMethodist College of Engineering \nand Technology\nHyderabad,Telangana, India\nV. Organizations around the globe are facing a growing arms race in cybersecurity as attackers employ advanced tools and tactics to breach networks, steal data, and interrupt operations. As a result, artificial intel -\nligence (AI) has become a game-changing factor, enabling companies to pre -\ndict, detect, and respond to threats with remarkable effectiveness [1]. This section examines the changes brought about by the transformative influence of AI on cybersecurity, emphasizing key applications, challenges, and future advancements necessary for creating secure digital environments.\n1.1.1   The Evolving Cybersecurity Landscape\nThe cybersecurity landscape has undergone significant changes over the past ten years, driven by the rapid growth in data generation, cloud technology, and interconnected devices. Traditional security approaches, which were once sufficient for mitigating basic malware or phishing attacks, now struggle to stay in sync with the intricate and advancing cyber threat environment. Attack vectors have expanded to target various systems, from critical infrastructure to individual devices, often utilizing automated and AI-enhanced techniques to bypass defenses. As organizations expand their digital footprint, they face a larger attack surface and threats that evolve in real time [2].\nThe increasing sophistication of cybercriminals has led to a rise in \nadvanced persistent threats (APTs), ransomware, and zero-day exploits. These attacks frequently evade conventional detection methods, underscor -\ning the necessity for innovative and adaptable security strategies. Relying on human intervention and rule-based frameworks is insufficient in this rapidly changing environment [3]. This necessitates a shift toward AI-based systems that are capable of examining large quantities of data, uncovering concealed patterns, and autonomously addressing emerging threats.Chapter 1\nArtificial Intelligence in \nCybersecurity\nFundamentals, Challenges, and Opportunities\nAguri Lydia Lois, C. Kishor Kumar Reddy, and \nMonika\xa0Singh\n\n2 AI-Driven Cybersecurity\n1.1.2   The Function of Artificial Intelligence in \nCybersecurity Defense\nAI is essential to modern cybersecurity, improving traditional security mea -\nsures through speed, precision, and adaptability. Machine learning (ML) \nalgorithms, a core aspect of AI, can quickly scan and analyze extensive data streams in actual time, recognizing irregularities and possible dangers faster than any human team could. Deep learning (DL) models, skilled at detect-ing complex patterns, are vital for finding malware, phishing attempts, and other cyber threats that evade conventional methods [4]. By automating these processes, AI enables organizations to shift from reactive approaches to proactive threat management. Figure\xa01.1 demonstrates that AI systems consistently observe and assess data to detect anomalies and initiate threat responses, thereby enhancing the cybersecurity process [5].\nBeyond threat detection, AI significantly contributes to incident response \nand vulnerability management. Automated systems powered by AI can pri-oritize vulnerabilities, recommend corrective actions, and execute predefined measures to counter attacks. In addition, organizations can leverage AI-driven predictive analytics to foresee possible threats by examining historical data and identifying trends. Despite its advantages, the use of AI in cyberse -\ncurity encounters challenges such as adversarial AI tactics and ethical con -\ncerns. This chapter highlights that addressing these challenges is essential for fully harnessing AI in the advancement of robust cybersecurity systems.\nData Collection\n(Logs, Traffic, User Behavior)\nData Analysis\n(Clearing Noise, Feature Extraction)\nThreat Detection\n(ML & DL Models for Identifying Threats)\nThreat Response\n(Automated Mitigation & Blocking)\nContinuous Learning\n(Feedback Loop to Improve Detection)\nThreat Intelligence Feedback\n(Insights for Further Prevention)\nFigure\xa01.1  AI-powered cyber defense workflow.\nArtificial Intelligence in Cybersecurity  3\n1.2  CORE CONCEPTS OF AI IN CYBERSECURITY\nArtificial intelligence is revolutionizing cybersecurity by examining large \ndatasets, recognizing intricate patterns, and automating responses. Key tech -\nniques such as ML, DL, and anomaly detection form the foundation of AI-based cybersecurity. These methods allow systems to evolve in response to emerging threats, detect harmful activities in real time, and enhance overall security strategies [6]. Each method offers unique capabilities for safeguard -\ning digital landscapes, focusing on different aspects of threat identification and response.\n1.2.1   Machine Learning for Identifying Threats\nML serves as a foundational component of AI in cybersecurity, facilitating the examination of large datasets and the accurate identification of mali -\ncious activities. Unlike traditional rule-based approaches, ML leverages data patterns and predictive models to adjust in real time to changing threats. Its ability to gain knowledge from past incidents and enhance identification mechanisms renders it vital for modern security infrastructures.\nAs shown in Figure\xa01.2, ML for threat detection involves two key phases: \ndata preparation and model training. In the preprocessing stage, large data -\nsets, often consisting of network logs, user activity records, and historical threat data, are cleaned and organized to ensure high-quality inputs for model development. Feature engineering is then applied to pinpoint crucial indicators of malicious behavior, such as unusual login times, irregular traf -\nfic levels, or deviations in user actions.\nData Collection\n(Network Logs, User Activity,  Historical Threat Data)\nData Preprocessing\n(Cleaning, Feature Engineering)\nModel Training\n(Supervised/Unsupervised Learning)\nThreat Detection\n(Identification of Malicious Activities)\nContinuous Learning/Improvement\n(Model Feedback & Updates)\nFigure\xa01.2  Machine learning workflow in threat detection.\n4 AI-Driven Cybersecurity\nModel training involves either supervised or unsupervised learning tech -\nniques. Table\xa01.1 provides a summary of various ML models and their appli -\ncations in cybersecurity. Supervised learning utilizes labeled data to instruct \nsystems on how to distinguish between safe and harmful activities [7]. For instance, models are trained on datasets consisting of known phishing emails and legitimate messages, enabling them to effectively classify future emails. By contrast, unsupervised learning does not rely on labeled data. It focuses on clustering and anomaly detection, identifying patterns that devi -\nate from the norm. Advanced models frequently combine these approaches to enhance detection performance.\nThe advantages of ML encompass the capability to process substantial \namounts of information, uncover zero-day vulnerabilities, and reduce reli -\nance on human intervention. However, challenges such as the necessity for expansive, high-quality datasets and vulnerability to adversarial attacks must be addressed. Despite these limitations, ML remains a crucial tool in bolstering cybersecurity efforts, allowing organizations to react to threats swiftly and efficiently.\n1.2.2   Deep Learning for Recognizing Patterns\nDL is a branch of ML and effectively uncovers complex patterns within large datasets, making it highly beneficial for identifying advanced cyber threats. By employing neural networks, DL models can analyze both struc -\ntured and unstructured data, such as logs, images, and audio, to uncover hidden patterns and anomalies.\nCybersecurity DL frameworks are developed using multilayer neural \nnetworks, which facilitate hierarchical data processing. In the context of malware detection, raw binary files are fed into convolutional neural Table\xa01.1  Types of Machine Learning Models for Threat Detection\nModel Type Description Use Case Advantages\nDecision Trees Supervised learning \nmodel using tree-like \nstructurePhishing detection Easy to interpret, \nhandles non-linear data\nNeural \nNetworksDeep learning models \nthat simulate human brainMalware \ndetection, pattern recognitionHigh accuracy, capable \nof learning complex patterns\nK-means \nClusteringUnsupervised learning \nfor clustering dataAnomaly detection \nin network trafficEfficient for large \ndatasets, finds hidden patterns\nSupport Vector \nMachinesSupervised \nmodel used for classificationSpam email \ndetectionEffective for small \ndatasets, robust to overfitting\nArtificial Intelligence in Cybersecurity  5\nnetworks (CNNs) that independently extract features, eliminating the \nneed for manual feature engineering [8]. The network layers identify intri -\ncate patterns, such as byte sequences or entropy measures, that indicate malicious behavior.\nDL is also applied in the detection of phishing scams. Recurrent neu -\nral networks (RNNs) assess email content and URLs for signs of phish-ing. These algorithms can effectively distinguish phishing attempts from legitimate emails by evaluating the context and arrangement of words. Additionally, autoencoders, a type of neural network, are frequently utilized for anomaly detection, recognizing data points that stray from established patterns.\nAs shown in Figure\xa01.3, DL processes raw data through specialized neural \nnetworks to identify patterns and anomalies. DL offers unparalleled accu-racy in pattern recognition and managing intricate datasets. However, it is resource-intensive and demands significant resources for training. Addi -\ntionally, DL models have the capability to be opaque, making it difficult to understand their results. Despite these challenges, DL remains a ground -\nbreaking method in cybersecurity, enabling advanced threat detection and prevention systems.Raw Data Input\n(Binary files, Emails, URLs)\nData Preprocessing\n(Cleaning, Organizing Data)\nFeature Extraction\n(Using CNNs, RNNs)\nModel Training\n(Training Neural Networks)\nThreat Detection\n(Malware, Phishing)\nContinuous Learning\n(Feedback, Model Improvement)\nFigure\xa01.3  Deep learning workflow in cyber threat detection.\n6 AI-Driven Cybersecur')

This comprehensive guide enables you to become a generative AI architect, \nbuilding powerful ChatGPT-grade systems from scratch that are adaptable to any platform. You’ll \ngo beyond basic chatbots, developing systems capable of semantic and sentiment analysis—with \ncontext-aware AI controllers at their core.\nYou’ll walk through the complete journey of designing an AI controller architecture with multi-user \nmemory retention, enabling the system to adapt to diverse user and system inputs. Building on \nthis foundation, you’ll architect a dynamic retrieval-augmented generation  (RAG ) system using \nPinecone, designed to intelligently combine instruction scenarios.\xa0\nWith powerful multimodal capabilities—including image generation, voice interactions, and \nmachine-driven reasoning—you’ll expand your system’s intelligence using chain-of-thought \norchestration to tackle the cross-domain automation challenges that real business environments \ndemand. You’ll also be fully equipped to integrate cutting-edge models such as OpenAI’s LLMs  \nand DeepSeek-R1 into your AI system—confident that it will remain stable, scalable, and  \nproduction-ready even in the turbulent pace of today’s AI ecosystem.\nBy the end, your generative AI system ( GenAISys ) will be capable of trajectory analysis and human \nmobility prediction, even when working with incomplete data. It will bring neuroscience-in -\nspired insight to your marketing messages, integrate seamlessly into human workflows, visualize \ncomplex delivery and movement scenarios, and connect to live external data—all wrapped in a \npolished, investor-ready interface.\nPreface xviii\nWho this book is for\nThis book is for AI and machine learning engineers, software architects, and enterprise developers \nseeking to architect and build a comprehensive GenAISys from scratch for enterprise applications. \nIt will particularly benefit those interested in building AI agents, creating advanced orchestration \nsystems, and leveraging AI for automation in marketing, production, and logistics. Software \narchitects and enterprise developers looking to build scalable AI-driven systems will also find \nimmense value in this guide. No prior superintelligence experience is necessary, but familiarity \nwith AI concepts is recommended.\nWhat this book covers\nChapter 1, Defining a Business-Ready Generative AI System, explains how to design robust, \nChatGPT-level AI systems tailored for business use, incorporating AI controllers, agents, con -\ntextual awareness, advanced memory retention, and strategic human collaboration. You will \nexplore how to go beyond basic model integrations to build AI solutions that deliver real-world \nbusiness results across industries and become an architect who can adapt to any environment.\nChapter 2 , Building the Generative AI Controller , dives into hands-on development of adaptive \nAI controllers, combining conversational agents and orchestrators. You’ll become proficient in \nbuilding a GenAISys that dynamically responds to user input, leverages advanced memory man-\nagement, and orchestrates tasks such as sentiment and semantic analysis, which are essential \nfor real-world, data-intensive applications.\nChapter 3 , Integrating Dynamic RAG into the GenAISys , teaches you how to architect a scalable, \ndynamic RAG system using Pinecone, effectively combining instruction scenarios and classical \ndata. You will discover how to build adaptable generative AI solutions capable of responding \nrapidly to real-world business disruptions and domain-specific challenges.\nChapter 4, Building the AI Controller Orchestration Interface, shows how to build a collaborative, \nevent-driven generative AI interface designed for rapid, real-world business responses. We’ll \ncreate a practical, multi-user conversational AI that integrates seamlessly into human workflows, \nenhancing decision-making during critical scenarios.\nChapter 5, Adding Multimodal, Multifunctional Reasoning with Chain of Thought, enhances our \nGenAISys with OpenAI’s powerful multimodal capabilities, including image generation, voice \ninteractions, and machine-driven reasoning. We’ll expand our system’s intelligence using chain-\nof-thought orchestration—enabling smart automation tailored to complex, cross-domain busi-\nness scenarios.\nPreface xix\nChapter 6, Reasoning E-Marketing AI Agents, harnesses the power of AI-driven memory analysis \nto create marketing messages customers remember. We’ll build a consumer memory agent that \nintelligently analyzes reviews and emotions, producing personalized marketing content enhanced \nby multimodal reasoning—bringing neuroscience insights directly into our GenAISys.\nChapter 7, Enhancing the GenAISys with DeepSeek , navigates the rapid evolution of AI without \ncompromising stability. You will learn how to strategically integrate cutting-edge models such \nas DeepSeek-R1 into our GenAISys, using a flexible handler selection mechanism—enabling our \nsystem to remain adaptable, scalable, and production-ready in a fast-changing market. \nChapter 8, GenAISys for Trajectory Simulation and Prediction, brings advanced AI-driven trajectory \nanalysis into our GenAISys to precisely predict human mobility and deliveries, even with incom-\nplete data. We’ll build an intuitive pipeline that leverages LLMs to simulate, analyze, and visualize \ncomplex delivery and movement scenarios, transforming spatial data into actionable insights. \nChapter 9 , Upgrading the GenAISys with Data Security and Moderation for Customer Service,  \nconnects our GenAISys securely to real-world data by integrating live weather information, travel  \ninformation, robust moderation tools, and advanced security features. You will discover how to \nsafely extend our AI’s capabilities beyond internal data, enabling personalized marketing, dynamic \nactivity recommendations, and real-time customer interactions.\nChapter 10, Presenting Your Business-Ready Generative AI System, will show you how to turn your \nGenAISys proof of concept into a compelling, investor-ready showcase. We’ll learn how to effec-\ntively present our AI system with clear messaging, practical demos, and a polished user interface, \ncapturing audience attention, demonstrating value, and proving readiness to scale in a crowded \nAI marketplace.\nTo get the most out of this book\nYou don’t need to be an AI expert to benefit from this guide, just some familiarity with the basics \nof artificial intelligence and programming. If you’ve worked with Python or explored LLMs like \nChatGPT, you’ll feel right at home.\nThis book introduces concepts like AI agent orchestration, memory retention, and RAG in clear, \nhands-on steps. Whether you’re a developer, engineer, or curious technologist, you’ll find tools, \ncode, and explanations designed to support real-world applications.\nNo deep math or theoretical background is required, only a desire to build meaningful AI systems \nthat solve business problems and scale in production environments.\nPreface xx\nThe code is available in Google Colab notebooks with automated installations or you can down-\nload the code locally.\nDownload the example code files\nThe code bundle for the book is hosted on GitHub at https://github.com/Denis2054/Building-\nBusiness-Ready-Generative-AI-Systems . We also have other code bundles from our rich catalog \nof books and videos available at https://github.com/PacktPublishing . Check them out!\nDownload the color images\nWe also provide a PDF file that has color images of the screenshots/diagrams used in this book. \nYou can download it here: https://packt.link/gbp/9781837020690 .\nConventions used\nThere are a number of text conventions used throughout this book.\nCodeInText : Indicates code words in text, database table names, folder names, filenames, file \nextensions, pathnames, dummy URLs, user input, and Twitter/X handles. For example: “Next, \nwe incorporate instruct_selector  into the existing interface layout ( VBox ).”\nA block of code is set as follows:\n# Ensure \'Instructions\' exists in the memory_selector options\ninstruct_selector = Dropdown(\n    options=[ "None","Analysis" , "Generation" ],\n    value= "None",  # Ensure def')

609\nxvpreface\nIf you’ve picked up this book, you’re probably aware of the extraordinary progress \nthat deep learning has brought to the field of artificial intelligence. In just a handful \nof years, we went from near-unusable computer vision and natural language process -\ning to highly performant systems deployed at scale in products you use every day. The \nconsequences of this sudden progress extend to almost every industry. Deep learning \nis applied to a diverse range of important problems across domains as different as med -\nical imaging, agriculture, autonomous driving, education, disaster prevention, and \nmanufacturing. Digital assistants are becoming pervasive on nearly every consumer \ncomputing device.\nYet, we believe deep learning is still in its early days. AI is going to represent a much \ngreater wave of disruption than anything that came before it. The technology will con -\ntinue to make its way to every problem where it can provide some utility—a transforma -\ntion that will take decades to play out. This is a transformation with profound societal \nimplications, on a global scale, spanning industries and cultures. We strongly believe \nthe only way to ensure such a transformation is beneficial for the people it will affect—\nall of us—is to radically democratize access to the underlying technology. We need to \nput understanding of deep learning—how it works, where it fails, and how to apply \nit—in the hands of as many people as possible, including people who aren’t researchers \nin the field.\nWhen I wrote the Keras deep learning framework in March 2015, the democratiza -\ntion of AI wasn’t what I had in mind. I had been doing research in machine learning \nfor several years and had built Keras to help with my own experiments. But since then, \nas newcomers have entered the field of deep learning, many have picked up Keras as \ntheir tool of choice. Accessibility quickly became an explicit goal in the development \nxvi preface xvi\nof Keras, and over the last decade, the Keras developer community has made remark -\nable progress in this area. We’ve put deep learning into the hands of millions of peo -\nple, who, in turn, are using it to solve problems that were, until recently, thought to be \nunsolvable.\nThe book you’re holding is another step on the way toward broadening access to the \nfield. We aim to make the concepts behind deep learning and their implementation as \napproachable as possible. Doing so doesn’t require watering anything down; we believe \nthat there are no difficult ideas in deep learning. This book will start with the very basics \nof the field and, layer by layer, build up to the cutting-edge generative AI models being \ndeployed today.\nThis is the third edition of Deep Learning with Python . In an effort to make this content \nas broadly available as possible, we are making this edition available for free, online at \nhttps: //deeplearningwithpython.io/ . We hope you will consider purchasing a physi -\ncal copy to support the project and read what we consider to be the best presentation \nof the content. This third edition amounts to a complete rewrite of the entire book, \nwith a broader introduction to today’s popular deep learning frameworks and greatly \nexpanded content on large generative AI models.\nWe hope this book proves valuable and helps you solve the problems that matter to \nyou.\nxviiacknowledgments\nFirst, we’d like to thank the Keras community for making this book possible. Over the \npast decade, Keras has grown to have thousands of open source contributors and more \nthan 2 million users. Their contributions and feedback have turned Keras into what it \nis today.\nOn a personal note, François would like to thank his wife for her endless support \nduring the development of Keras and the writing of this book. Matthew would like to \nthank his partner Kate, his family, and all the friends who have supported him along the \nway.\nWe thank the people at Manning who made this book possible: publisher Marjan \nBace and everyone on the editorial and production teams, including Michael Stephens, \nAleksandar Dragosavljevi ć, and many others who worked behind the scenes.\nMany thanks go to the peer reviewers: Aakash Nain, Abheesht Sharma, Abhishek \nShivanna, Aritra Roy Gosthipaty, Avinash Tiwari, Brandon Friar, Christopher Kardell, \nSrivathsan Srinivasagopalan, Edmon Begoli, Guillaume Alleon, Ian Stirk, Jacqueline \nNolis, Kishore Reddy, Levi McClenny, Margaret Maynard-Reid, Nilson Chapagain, \nPrashanth Josyula, Preetish Kakkar, Sai Srinivas Somarouthu, Samuel Marks, Srivathsan \nSrinivasagopalan, Thiago Britto Borges, Todd Cook, and Varun Chawla—and all the \nother people who sent us feedback on the draft of the book.\nOn the coding side, special thanks go to Tomasz Kalinowski, who contributed to \ncode examples in this book; Ian Hough, who served as the book’s development editor; \nand Gabriel Rasskin, who served as the book’s technical proofreader.\nxviiiabout this book\nThis book was written for anyone who wishes to explore deep learning from scratch or \nbroaden their understanding of deep learning. Whether you’re a practicing machine \nlearning engineer, a software developer, or a college student, you’ll find value in these \npages.\nYou’ll explore deep learning in an approachable way—starting simply and working \nup to state-of-the-art techniques. We hope you’ll find that this book strikes a balance \nbetween intuition, theory, and hands-on practice. It avoids mathematical notation, pre -\nferring instead to explain the core ideas of deep learning via functioning code paired \nwith explanations of the underlying principles. You’ll train machine learning models \nfrom scratch in a number of different problem domains and learn practical recommen -\ndations for writing deep learning programs and deploying them in the real world.\nAfter reading this book, you’ll have a solid understanding of what deep learning is, \nwhen it’s applicable, and what its limitations are. You’ll be familiar with the standard \nworkflow for approaching and solving machine learning problems, and you’ll know \nhow to address commonly encountered issues.\nWho should read this book\nThis book is written for people with some Python programming experience who want \nto get started with machine learning and deep learning. But this book can also be valu -\nable to many different types of readers:\n¡\tIf you’re a data scientist familiar with machine learning, this book will provide \nyou with a solid, practical introduction to deep learning, the fastest-growing and \nmost significant subfield of machine learning.\n xix about  this book  xix\n¡\tIf you’re a deep learning researcher or practitioner looking to get started with \nthe Keras framework, you’ll find this book to be the ideal Keras crash course.\n¡\tIf you’re a graduate student studying deep learning in a formal setting, you’ll \nfind this book to be a practical complement to your education, helping you build \nintuition around the behavior of deep neural networks and familiarizing you \nwith key best practices.\nEven technically minded people who don’t code regularly will find this book useful as \nan introduction to both basic and advanced deep learning concepts.\nTo understand the code examples, you’ll need reasonable Python proficiency. You \ndon’t need previous experience with machine learning or deep learning: this book cov -\ners, from scratch, all the necessary basics. You don’t need an advanced mathematics \nbackground either—high-school-level mathematics should suffice to follow along.\nHow this book is organized: A road map\nThis book contains 20 chapters, organized as follows:\n¡\tChapters 1–7: Foundations of deep learning —These chapters give you a solid ground -\ning in deep learning. We discuss the history of the field, provide an introduction \nto coding with the major deep learning frameworks currently available (JAX, \nPyTorch, and TensorFlow), and outline a practical guide to applying machine \nlearning to real-world problems. We look closely at the Keras library for training \nmachine learning models.\n¡\tChapters 8–12: Computer vision —These chapters cover machine learning on image \ndata. We train models to classify entire images and models to recognize and sepa -\nrate out individual objects in images. We look closely at ConvNets, a model archi -\ntecture well suited to images and the first big success of the deep learning era.\n¡\tChapter 13: Timeseries forecasting —This chapter covers working with timeseries \ndata. We take data that is measured over time, like the weather or sales data, and \nuse past patterns to predict future trends.\n¡\tChapters 14–15: Natural language processing —These chapters cover applying deep \nlearning to text. We build sentiment classifiers to predict whether text is posi -\ntive or negative. We build an English-to-Spanish translation model. We pay spe -\ncial attention to the Transformer, a popular model architecture particularly well \nsuited to text modeling.\n¡\tChapters 16–17: Generative modeling —These chapters are all about using deep \nlearning to create new content. We work with models that can produce new \nimages and text as output. We discuss chatbots like ChatGPT and image gener -\nation systems. We both train generative models from scratch and use larger pre -\ntrained models trained on large amounts of data over weeks or months.\n¡\tChapters 18–20: Conclusions —The final chapters of this book tie together what \nwe have learned. We explore practical engineering concerns with deep learn -\ning systems. We dedicate a chapter to exploring potential futures for the field \nxx about  this book xx\nand identifying new research directions, and then review the concepts presented \nacross the book.\nAbout the code \nThis book is an example of literate programming—it is simultaneously a prose expla -\nnation of deep learning concepts and a runnable Python program. Starting with chap -\nter 2, each chapter will be interspersed with code listings that can be run as a Jupyter \nnotebook, an interactive notebook for running Python code and visualizing data. We \nstrongly suggest running, modifying, and playing with the examples in this book as you \nread to build your own intuitions on the concepts presented.\nAll code is written in the Python language with the deep learning library Keras. Keras \ncan be run on top of TensorFlow, PyTorch, and JAX, the most popular low-level deep \nlearning frameworks as of 2025. All code can be run on a local machine or directly in \nthe browser using Google Colab, a hosted environment for Jupyter notebooks.\nYou can get executable snippets of code from the liveBook version of this book, \nincluded with your print or eBook purchase, at https: //livebook.manning.com/book/\ndeep-learning-with-python-third-edition . The complete code for the examples in the \nbook is available for download from the Manning website at https: //www.manning  \n.com/books/deep-learning-with-python-third-edition  and on GitHub, at https: //\ngithub.com/fchollet/deep-learning-with-python-notebooks , along with instructions \nfor')

Through \nreal-world case studies, practical strategies, and in-depth discussions, this book illus -\ntrates how organizations can leverage AI to accelerate Lean transformation, enhance human performance, and drive sustainable growth. Readers will gain actionable knowledge on integrating AI with Lean tools such as 5S, poka-yoke, single minute exchange of dies, total productive maintenance, and value stream mapping, among others. The book also highlights the critical role of leadership and culture in ensuring AI-driven Lean implementations uplift rather than replace human capabilities.\nThis book is designed for forward-thinking innovators, business leaders, Lean prac -\ntitioners, and AI enthusiasts eager to explore the synergy between technology and \nhuman-centric process improvement. Whether you are an executive driving digital transformation, a Lean expert looking to modernize methodologies, or a professional seeking to understand AI’s role in operational excellence, this book provides a stra -\ntegic guide to mastering Lean-AI integration. It is an essential read for those ready to challenge conventional paradigms and embrace the future of efficiency, collabora -\ntion, and intelligent innovation.\nContinuous Improvement Series\nSeries Editors: Elizabeth A. Impacts on Learning and Skill Development\n................................... 242\nIndex  ...................................................................................................................... 247\n\nviiForeword 1\nThe rapid rise of Generative AI (GenAI), which has democratized access to the \npower of AI’s predictive and decisioning capabilities, is revolutionizing every sphere of business. Companies no longer need to invest millions in experimental and unre -\nliable AI solutions that require years to implement and deliver value. With the cloud-based on-tap services of various GenAI platforms, companies can choose and deploy the right model that meets the needs of their use case and business appetite. Barely two years into the advent of GenAI, its industrial applications are multiplying at an incredible pace, offering a plethora of scenarios and options for solving different types of operational and business challenges. And yet GenAI is just an early precur -\nsor to the even more powerful and expansive artificial general intelligence (AGI), which is eventually going to subsume every aspect of running a business. The advent of AGI will happen gradually and then suddenly, just as GenAI burst onto every -\none’s consciousness seemingly out of nowhere. In reality, the groundwork for GenAI was laid over the previous decade, but the progress was incremental until OpenAI’s GPT3 was uncloaked in November 2022. Based on a revolutionary transformer model, this large language model (LLM) could interpret regular conversations and churn out human-like responses by crunching terabytes of data in a fraction of a second. It could rapidly answer a plethora of questions or solve complex problems through conversational prompts while also handling multi-modal inputs and outputs producing amazing graphics and videos. Like many of the technologies preceding it, the adoption of GenAI initially started with programmers and then leapfrogged into the realm of the average non-technical consumer of content and media who found a perfect digital companion that could handle multifarious tasks from writing a poem to solving a math homework assignment. The biggest advancement of this disruptive technology is that it provided access to the endless power of hyper-scaled computing fed on petabytes of data to the average person who doesn’t have to learn any special skill or programming language other than mastering the art of prompt engineering. GenAI is now advancing into every aspect of one’s life and work by unleashing the power of co-pilots and agents that can perform mundane tasks as well as enable synchronous workflows that remove inefficiencies within business functions. This heralds the age of AI where literally every idea can be transformed into action and the art of the possible is within everyone’s reach.\nMany have been talking about the advent of Industry 5.0, which extends the 4.0 \nparadigm to add a human edge – a truly autonomous world of seamlessly intercon-nected devices and machines that can operate end-to-end functions like a worker, but without human intervention. With the convergence between AI, IoT, and auto -\nmation, this vision is becoming a reality very rapidly. While there is a fundamental dichotomy between the deterministic accuracy of machines and the probabilistic abstractions of AI, by using the right guardrails and frameworks, the two can come together to deliver solutions that are Industry 5.0 level. Quite counter-intuitively, AI can bring the human back into the machines by providing a layer of sentient deci -\nsions and actions that can appear to be almost humanoid. The recent emergence of \nviii Foreword 1\nAgentic AI and Empathic AI is furthering this paradigm shift by taking on roles \nthat think, act, and emote in a way similar to how human beings would react to cer -\ntain conversations or situations. This opens up the possibility of more human-like machines and bots that don’t just follow a calculating prescriptive path but adopt a more human-centered and dynamically adaptive approach to solving problems or finishing tasks. That is one of the wonders of self-learning heuristic AI algorithms, which become smarter as well as “self-aware” through feedback and continuous improvement. The successful use of AI to power a hyper-personalized and dig -\nitally seamless future requires that Empathic AI remains an integral element of any AI system. But the biggest challenge to ensuring that AI and humans can work harmoniously is actually in the leadership that decides how to blend them within the value chains. Incorporating AI and machine learning (ML) into machines and processes just for the sake of doing it provides no sustainable benefit. Decisions regarding job displacement, redefining and retooling skill sets, and transparency in complex decision-making are very contextual and impact the business and social outcomes – they are the true indicators of the successful deployment of AI. The age of AI requires a new approach to leadership and design of systems – one that strives for a balance between business and human values. All the tools and methods are at our disposal. It’s for us to decide – do we consciously steer toward a more utopian future where AI is seamlessly embedded within our work and lives or do we let technology take control and shape a dystopian reality, which disrupts and distances us from who we are.\nLean and operational excellence is a discipline that has been addressed through -\nout Industry 2.0 and 3.0. It took a backseat during 4.0 as the general assumption was that we had reached its peak and further productivity gains would be through technology (including automation and analytics). But the advent of AI is opening up a vista of opportunities to not only take Lean to a new level but also eliminate some of its drawbacks and alleviate the human impact. At the surface, Lean with its structured and deterministic approach seems to conflict with AI’s inherent traits of probabilistic, ambiguous, and sometimes inaccurate results. But a deeper look reveals how AI could fundamentally fix some of the most significant disadvantages of Lean, such as supply chain risks of just-in-time production or worker burnout and dissatisfaction. Lean and AI can come together to drive productivity and quality significantly higher while humanizing operational excellence by reducing the stress of process rigor and repetitive tasks. Workers who fear the job displacement impact of AI should actually see this as the solution to improving their day-to-day workflow and enhancing the net value of their job functions. AI in fact is the perfect compan -\nion for a worker, aiding and performing actions, detecting errors, and pre-empting downstream issues in a value chain.\nThis book is an eye-opening look into the potential convergence of Lean and AI. \nIt delves into the different aspects and ways of balancing innovation and process discipline to unleash new productivity. It will show business strategists as well as operational executives how to bring Lean and AI together to power next-level inno -\nvation and value in any industry. How to mitigate the negative perceptions of AI and instead leverage it as the digital copilot that can improve everyone’s work lives. \nix Foreword 1\nAnd very importantly, how to enable sustainability and scalability in an increas-\ningly resource-scarce world. Lean-AI should be required reading for anyone who wants to solve the eternal conundrum of achieving perfection with inspiration, in any field of life.\nAnupam Govil\nFounder and Chief AI Evangelist, Austin AI Valley\nManaging Partner, Avasant\n\nxiForeword 2\nWhen asked to give a presentation at a conference, the most common topic I\xa0am \nasked to present is Technology and the Shingo Model. In the 30+ years of adminis-tering the Shingo Prize, the Shingo Institute has had a lot of opportunities to see the best organizations in the world.\nOne thing we have consistently noticed is that one of the big reasons these organi -\nzations are the best is because they are the best at adopting new technologies. When comparing these organizations to their competition, we often see they achieve much better productivity with significantly lower investments in technology. It isn’t that they are not making investments in technology – they are. But they avoid wasteful investments in technology.\nWe attribute the difference between this effective use of technology to people \nand their behaviors. In other words, to their superior culture. The example to all of us is provided by Toyota and the development of jidōka. For those unfamiliar with \nthis term, jid ōka is the Japanese word for automation. It is written in the kanji as \n自動化 . Except in Toyota, they created their own word for automation where they \nsubstitute the middle character ( 動), with a different character with the same pronun -\nciation (働). The difference between the standard automation and the Toyota version \nof automation is called a ninben  (the addition on the left-hand side of the character) \nwhich signifies a person. Hence, Toyota often refers to their version of automation as “automation with a human touch.”\nThe implementation of any technology requires a human touch. Matter of fact, it \nrequires more than just a touch, it requires human involvement. Humans ensure that technology is adopted purposefully and is informed by correct principles.\nIn the Shingo Model , the human aspect of technology is emphasized through the \nShingo Guiding Principle of Respect Every Individual . Humans decide how tech-\nnology can make improvements. Humans implement technology in the process. Humans confirm the effectiveness of technology after implementation. The Guiding Principle demands that the role of humans be respected. The Guiding Principles in the Shingo Model are designed to be interactive. For example, respecting every individual while  improving flow. Dr. Dalal and Dr. Cudney do an excellent job of \ndescribing the Shingo Model , the role of humans in the improvement process, and \nhow technologies can help humans achieve improvement.\nLeaders cannot ignore the potential revolutionary impact of – artificial intelli -\ngence (AI). In this book, the authors do an excellent job of tackling what will prob -\nably be the most transformative technology of all. They do so by setting the proper context of the purposeful implementation of AI as led by humans. They build on that theme by providing several examples of practical improvements that AI could generate.\nDr. Dalal and Dr. Cudney demonstrate that purposeful adoption of technology \ncan reduce waste, reduce defects, shorten lead times, and improve productivity. One \nxii Foreword 2\nimportant reason why the best-performing companies in the world are the best is \nbecause they are very good at implementing new technologies. The same will be true with AI.\nKen Snyder\nExecutive Director\nShingo Institute\nxiiiPreface\nWe stand at the threshold of a profound transformation. The convergence of Lean \nprinciples with artificial intelligence (AI) is not merely an evolution, it is a revolution in how we work, lead, and innovate. Lean-AI: A\xa0Humanistic Integration of Lean and AI is more than a book; it is a call to action for leaders, practitioners, and visionaries \nwho recognize that the future is not just about automation but about the seamless integration of human ingenuity with technological advancement.\nRooted in efficiency, waste reduction, and continuous improvement, Lean meth -\nodologies have long been a cornerstone of operational excellence. Now, combined with AI’s dynamic capabilities, they usher in a new era of agility, intelligence, and resilience. While Lean principles provide the strategic compass for culture transfor -\nmation, AI serves as the engine driving us into uncharted territories of innovation and competence. Together, they redefine what is possible.\nThis book is a guide for navigating this intricate interplay – one that goes beyond \nstreamlining processes to shaping the very essence of our workplaces. It is about more than just efficiency; it is about how technology influences leadership, collabo -\nration, and the formation of a future-ready, technology-savvy culture.\nBoth authors of this pioneering work, Adil Dalal and Dr. Beth Cudney, have been \nat the forefront of Lean and Six Sigma innovation, earning prestigious accolades, including the Shingo Research and Publication Medal and the ASQ Philip Crosby Medal. Their work has transformed industries and shaped the evolution of opera -\ntional excellence.\nAI is not an isolated force but a transformative ally. When guided by ethical and \nhumanistic leadership, AI does not replace human potential – it elevates it. This is the essence of Lean-AI: not just about optimization, but about purpose, culture, and ensuring that AI serves humanity, not the other way around.\nAI’s influence on cognition, creativity, and development must be handled with \ncare – an imperative that extends beyond individuals to entire organizations. This book ensures that AI enhances the core values of Lean rather than eroding them, fostering workplaces that are not only more innovative and agile but also deeply human-centric.\nMore than a guide, this book is a manifesto for the next frontier of operational \nexcellence. Through compelling case studies, real-world applications, and a bold vision for Industry 5.0+, we demonstrate how Lean-AI is the key to thriving in the digital era. Expect practical insights, transformative ideas, and moments of reve -\nlation as we journey through the landscape of Lean, AI, and the cultural shift that binds them.\nIf you are ready to challenge the status quo and harness AI to elevate – not \nreplace – human values, join us on this journey. Let’s ensure that AI strengthens our principles, enriches our workplaces, and redefines excellence for the future.\nBuckle up – Lean-AI is here to revolutionize the way we work, think, and lead.\n\nxvAuthors\nAdil Dalal is the President and CEO of Pinnacle Process Solutions, Intl, LLC, hold -\ning two master’s degrees and a doctorate in business administration and several cer -\ntifications in leadership, coaching, quality, Lean, Six Sigma, project management, \nand digital transformations. She holds eight ASQ certifications, which include ASQ Certified Quality Engineer, Manager of Quality/Operational Excellence, and Certified Six Sigma Black Belt, among others.\nDOI: 10.1201/9781003532972-1  1Lean Landscape\nHISTORY OF LEAN\nManufacturing has continued to evolve from an individual product crafted by an \nartisan to highly standardized, yet customizable, mass production. Before the 1900s, products were handcrafted by artisans. Typically, artisans were skilled craftspeople who made each product one at a time from start to completion; therefore, produc -\ntion speed was generally slow, and there were inconsistencies in the final products (Mourtzis\xa0& Doukas, 2014 ). Quality was high because the focus was on that one \nproduct. However, there was considerable variation from product to product and in the process because a process step from one product to the following product might be several weeks apart. In addition, artisan training was inconsistent because it largely relied on apprenticeships for training rather than standardized, formal training that was consistent across a field. Therefore, product variation among different artisans was inconsistent. Further, the lack of standardization also meant that the same arti -\nsan could not produce the same part repeatability in terms of product dimensions across their products.\nEarly industrialization in the 1800s and early 1900s introduced mechanized pro -\nduction, which enabled organizations to produce higher volumes of products with lower variation; however, production planning was manual ( Marsh, 2012 ).\nIn 1913, Henry Ford introduced the moving assembly line, which led to mass \nproduction and reduced costs. Machines performed single tasks. One operator was responsible for the process at each machine or station. Therefore, batch production became the dominant production method. This resulted in single-task orientation and more standardized training on specific tasks. Production was high volume, and management focused on high machine utilization. Subsequently, there were large production lots and high inventory. However, the singular task activities resulted in little variation in the process and product ( Black\xa0& Hunter, 2003 ). Since the assembly \nline used batch production, lead times were long because each item in the batch had to wait for all products in that batch to be completed before it continued to the next step in the process ( Mikati, 2010 ).\nIn the 1950s, Toyota developed the Toyota Production System (TPS), which \nfocused on Just-in-Time (JIT) manufacturing and producing products based on cus -\ntomer demand. TPS also included numerous continuous improvement principles to reduce waste and increase efficiency ( Ohno, 1982 ).\nBy the 1970s and 1990s, Toyota formalized the Lean manufacturing principles, \nincluding methods such as value stream mapping (VSM) and continuous flow to improve production efficiency ( Smith\xa0& Vidal, 2019 ). In the 1990s and early 2000s, \norganizations began integrating Six Sigma and Lean methodologies to improve pro -\ncesses by reducing variation and waste ( Gupta et al., 2020 ). While the Lean meth -\nodology began in manufacturing, organizations began applying Lean in service 1\n2 Lean-AI\nindustries, healthcare, finance, and administrative functions to improve operational \nefficiency.\nThe Lean principles have continued to evolve to incorporate the principles of \nIndustry 4.0. This has led to the integration of Lean with digital technologies, arti -\nficial intelligence (AI), and automation for predictive maintenance, smart manufac -\nturing, and real-time process optimization ( Kumar et al., 2021 ). Organizations use \nthis integrated approach to leverage data analytics and machine learning to further optimize efficiency and decision-making processes.\nFigure\xa0 1.1  illustrates the timeline of these key developments in manufacturing \nsystems.\nTHE TRADITIONAL MANUFACTURING ENVIRONMENT\nTraditional manufacturing uses verbal production instructions and is still in use today. This type of manufacturing system is based on forecasting and, as a result, requires frequent changes by manufacturing planners. In this environment, organi -\nzations produce and schedule production at many locations, with little coordination. Therefore, inventory and materials are decentralized and difficult to control. Pro -\nduction supplies are bought ')

It addresses the pressing issue of data protection in the context of \nGenerative Pre‑trained Transformer (GPT) technology, emphasizing the EU’s com ‑\nmitment to individual privacy rights. This book also evaluates AI’s role in public \ngovernance, using Albania as a case study, and examines the potential of blockchain \ntechnology in enhancing legal processes. The ethical nuances surrounding AI’s inte ‑\ngration into legal systems are critically examined, particularly regarding algorithmic \nbias and human oversight. This book advocates for a collaborative approach involv ‑\ning legal experts and data scientists to navigate these complexities effectively.\nThis book is a key resource for postgraduate students, researchers, and legal pro ‑\nfessionals seeking to better understand the benefits and risks of incorporating AI into \nlegal practice.\n\nArtificial Intelligence in  \nLegal Systems\nBridging Law and  \nTechnology through AI\nEdited by\nEriona Çela, Narasimha Rao Vajjhala,  \nand Behrouz Aslani\nDesigned cover image: Shutterstock\nFirst edition published 2026\nby CRC Press\n2385 NW Executive Center Drive, Suite 320, Boca Raton FL 33431\nand by CRC Press\n4 Park Square, Milton Park, Abingdon, Oxon, OX14 4RN\nCRC Press is an imprint of Taylor & Francis Group, LLC\n© 2026 selection and editorial matter, Eriona Çela, Narasimha Rao Vajjhala, and Behrouz Aslani; \nindividual chapters, the contributors\nReasonable efforts have been made to publish reliable data and information, but the author and \npublisher cannot assume responsibility for the validity of all materials or the consequences of \ntheir use. Among these, the legal system stands out as a sector where the potential \nfor transformation is tremendous, although it includes a lot of challenges. With the \nemergence of Artificial Intelligence (AI), we are witnessing a chance to redefine how \njustice is administered, accessed, and understood.\nWhat fascinates me most about AI in the legal sector is its capacity to address \nlong‑standing challenges: accelerating legal research, enhancing decision‑making \nprocesses, and widening access to justice for the underprivileged. These possibilities \nconnect strongly with the ideas of social computing, using technology to increase \ncooperation and accessibility, and emerging technologies, where innovation fosters \nempowerment and understanding. AI in legal systems examines how these concepts \nmerge to build more equitable and efficient legal systems.\nThis book addresses AI’s potential not simply as a tool for efficiency but as a \ncatalyst for systemic transformation. From natural language processing in docu ‑\nment review to predictive analytics in case outcomes, the examples provided here \nhighlight how AI may supplement the skills of legal practitioners. Yet, as someone \nstrongly interested in understanding the social elements of technology, I am equally \ndrawn to this book’s reflections on ethics, transparency, and the risks of biases. These \nchallenges are crucial as we work toward developing AI‑driven systems that reflect \nand support societal standards and norms.\nWhat is most noticeable is this book’s emphasis on education and skill‑building \nfor legal practitioners. As AI becomes a cornerstone of modern legal systems, train ‑\ning practitioners with the skills to efficiently and ethically take advantage of these \ntools will be critical. This aligns with the concept of social computing and emerging \ntechnologies, where the focus is on enabling individuals to navigate and excel in an \nincreasingly digital society.\nAI in legal systems is more than a discussion of technological potential; it is a \ncomprehensive guide to ensuring that innovation serves humanity. It bridges the gap \nbetween law and technology, demonstrating how interdisciplinary collaboration can \nlead to substantial advancements. For readers from the disciplines of education, tech‑\nnology, and law, this book offers not just insights but also a vision for how AI could \nenhance one of society’s most fundamental institutions.\nAs you engage with the ideas and case studies presented in this book, I encourage \nyou to think about how your own expertise, whether in law, technology, or education, \ncan contribute to this transformative journey. The future of AI in legal systems is a \ncollaborative endeavor, and this book offers an exciting foundation for making that \nfuture more just, inclusive, and impactful.\nVasileios Paliktzoglou\nviii Foreword\nABOUT THE FOREWORD AUTHOR\nDr.\xa0Vasileios Paliktzoglou  is an academic and industry professional who holds a \nPh.D. in Computer Science from the University of Eastern Finland. He is an active \ncontributor to academia, serving as a guest and associate editor for prestigious \njournals such as the Journal of Information Systems Education ( JISE ) and IAFOR \nJournal of Education . He has been a keynote speaker at several academic and indus‑\ntry events, sharing his insights on social computing, collaborative learning, and \nemerging technologies in higher education. Dr.\xa0Paliktzoglou also actively partici ‑\npates in international research projects, highlighting his commitment to advancing \nknowledge and innovation as the Book Series Editor for “Emerging Technologies \nin Education” at Vernon Press and “AI and Education” at STAR Scholars Press. \nHis expertise continues to shape the academic and research landscape at Bahrain \nPolytechnic.\nix\nPreface\nArtificial Intelligence in Legal Systems is a timely exploration of how artificial intel ‑\nligence (AI) is transforming the legal field in the midst of a global digital revolution. \nAs technology continues to redefine industries and societal functions, the legal sys‑\ntem, a cornerstone of governance and justice, faces unique challenges and opportuni ‑\nties brought about by AI. This book seeks to bridge the gap between technological \nadvancements and the ethical, procedural, and practical demands of the legal profes‑\nsion. Through its comprehensive chapters, this book delves into AI’s multifaceted \nimpact on legal systems. It examines AI’s capabilities to automate routine tasks, ana‑\nlyze large datasets, and streamline case management, while also addressing critical \nissues such as transparency, accountability, and ethical dilemmas. By presenting a \nbalanced view of the promises and perils of AI integration, this book provides a \nroadmap for legal practitioners, policymakers, and scholars to navigate this complex \nlandscape.\nA significant portion of this book focuses on the European Union’s approach to \nregulating AI in the legal domain. It provides an in‑depth analysis of the EU’s legal \nframeworks and explores the challenges posed by integrating AI tools, such as algo ‑\nrithmic bias, data privacy concerns, and ethical considerations in decision‑making. \nBeyond the EU, this book incorporates perspectives from other regions, offering a \nglobal view of AI’s impact on legal systems and the shared struggles to ensure fair ‑\nness and justice in an era of rapid technological change. This book also advocates for \na collaborative approach to AI adoption, emphasizing the importance of aligning AI \ntools with the needs of legal professionals and the broader goals of justice. By tailor ‑\ning AI to specific legal contexts and judicial processes, contributors demonstrate how \nthis technology can enhance efficiency and decision‑making while preserving the \nfoundational values of the legal system. Practical strategies and case studies further \nillustrate how AI can address complex legal challenges while maintaining integrity \nand accountability.\nArtificial Intelligence in Legal Systems serves as both a guide and a critical \nresource for those at the forefront of legal innovation. It equips readers with the \ninsights needed to harness AI responsibly, balancing its transformative potential with \nthe ethical imperatives of justice and fairness. Legal professionals will find action ‑\nable recommendations for integrating AI into their practice, while policymakers and \nscholars will gain a deeper understanding of the regulatory and societal implica‑\ntions of AI in law. Ultimately, this book underscores the importance of thoughtful \nand ethical AI integration in the legal system. It seeks to empower its readers to not \nonly embrace technological advancements but also to safeguard the principles of \ntransparency, equity, and accountability that underpin the rule of law. As the legal \nfield continues to evolve in the face of AI’s transformative power, this book provides \na vital framework for navigating its complexities and opportunities with confidence \nand clarity.\nBehrouz Aslani  \nNarasimha Rao Vajjhala\nx\nAcknowledgments\nThe journey of editing this book Artificial Intelligence in Legal Systems has been \nboth enlightening and profoundly rewarding, and we extend our heartfelt gratitude \nto those who contributed to this work. As AI con ‑\ntinues to permeate legal practices and governance structures, its implications for \nefficiency, transparency, accountability, and justice demand thorough exploration.\n1.2  AI IN THE LEGAL SECTOR: OPPORTUNITIES \nAND CHALLENGES\nAI’s integration into the legal system offers unprecedented opportunities to stream ‑\nline operations and improve outcomes. Legal professionals now leverage AI tools to \nmanage routine tasks, such as document review, legal research, case management, \nand predictive analytics. By utilizing Machine Learning (ML) and Natural Language \nProcessing (NLP) technologies, lawyers, judges, and other legal practitioners are \nequipped to process complex data with remarkable accuracy and speed, enabling \nthem to focus on nuanced legal analysis and decision‑making.\nDespite these advancements, the legal sector’s adoption of AI is fraught with chal ‑\nlenges. Ethical concerns about algorithmic bias, the erosion of human judgment, and \ndata privacy issues highlight the need for regulatory and ethical oversight. These \nconcerns are particularly critical in contexts where justice, fairness, and account ‑\nability are at stake.\n1.3 SCOPE AND OBJECTIVES OF THIS BOOK\nThis book delves into the transformative role of AI in the legal system, balancing an \nexploration of its potential benefits with an analysis of the ethical and legal dilemmas \nit introduces. By examining case studies, regulatory frameworks, and technological \ninnovations worldwide, this book provides a comprehensive understanding of how \nAI can be responsibly integrated into the legal profession.\n1\n DOI: 10.1201/9781003541899-1\n2 Artificial Intelligence in Legal Systems\nThe overarching objective is to foster a balanced discourse, guiding policymakers, \nlegal practitioners, and scholars through the complexities of AI adoption in the legal \nsystem. This approach ensures that technological advancements enhance, rather than \nundermine, the principles of justice, fairness, and accountability.\n1.4 ORGANIZATION OF THIS BOOK\nThis book is structured into 13 chapters, each focusing on critical aspects of AI’s role \nin the legal system. The first chapter introduces this book and summarizes the topics \ndiscussed. Other chapters offer a holistic perspective on AI’s transformative impact \nin modern legal practice and governance.\n1.4.1  Artifici Al intelligence  in the legAl Sector : Applic Ation S, ethic Al \nchAllengeS , And legAl concern S under  europe An union lAw\nChapter 2 examines the significant transformation of the legal profession through \nthe increasing adoption of AI systems, which range from handling administrative \ntasks to performing complex legal analyses. It emphasizes the dual nature of AI’s \nimpact—offering substantial efficiency gains while also raising critical ethical and \nlegal challenges, particularly regarding transparency and liability. Ultimately, the \nchapter underscores the necessity for further legal analysis of these emerging issues \nwithin the context of the EU’s AI Regulation 2024/1689, highlighting their impor ‑\ntance for contemporary legal scholarship and practice.\n1.4.2  e urope An union’S perSpective  on protection  of \nperSon Al dAtA in the erA of gpt t echnology\nChapter 3 analyzes the European Union’s leadership in the advancement of Generative \nPre‑trained Transformer (GPT) technology while emphasizing the importance of safe ‑\nguarding personal data. It focuses on the complexities of the EU legal framework as it \nstrives to balance innovation in Generative Artificial Intelligence with the protection \nof individual privacy rights, exploring the moral, legal, and societal implications of \nthis technology. It \nfocuses on fine‑tuning SaulLM using the Low‑Rank Adaptation Technique (LoRA) \non an Indian legal dataset to create NLP systems capable of performing com ‑\nplex judicial tasks, such as semantic segmentation and legal statute identification. \nAdditionally, the chapter emphasizes the importance of making this model publicly \naccessible via HuggingFace to support accessible justice and timely decision‑mak ‑\ning in the legal domain.\n1.4.6  Applic Ation of Artifici Al intelligence  in the \nindiAn legAl SyStem: proS And conS \nChapter 7 investigates the transformative role of AI in the legal system, highlight ‑\ning its ability to enhance efficiency, accuracy, and accessibility in legal practices. Over these years, the entities have had an \nevolving relationship, and gaining insights from this evolving relationship has become \nessential. Graph Mining: Practical Uses and Instruments for Exploring Complex Networks \nattempts to ﬁll this gap by being a one-stop shop for anyone looking for an accessible \nintroduction to graph mining from well-known contributors in their respective ﬁelds. \nWe wrote this book because we believe a concrete but informal textbook linking theory \nto practice in graph mining is sorely lacking. These concepts are outlined in a clear, take-\nit-to-the-bank format, with theoretical foundations supported by practical stories and case \nstudies. This includes a thorough introduction to graph representation, graph traversal \nalgorithms, and community detection techniques to analyze real-world phenomena. This \nwill provide readers with a strong foundation to tackle advanced challenges in ﬁelds such as bioinformatics, social network analysis, and ﬁnancial data analysis. \nWorking with authors who come from such diverse backgrounds means that we can \ndraw on a variety of experiences and points of view to give our readers a well-rounded \nunderstanding of the materials. We hope that this book becomes a valuable resource for \nresearchers looking to expand their understanding of graph mining and investigate new \nstrategies for revealing hidden patterns in complex data systems. \nWe thank our families, colleagues, and institutions for their continual support (ﬁnan-\ncial, emotional, and otherwise) while we were writing this book. We sincerely thank \nSpringer for this opportunity to support the academic and professional community through\nvii\nviii Preface\nthe publication of this book as well.
